  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_bb9706a7-91ae-4f97-a20d-011277e1018c'
      });

  <span id="freeText8537661853797962106" style="display:none">A gripping thriller from the Richard and Judy award-winning author of Girl, Missing, Sophie McKenzie.<br /><br />When Theo discovers the father he thought died when he was a baby is still alive, he's determined to find him. There, they both make some startling discoveries about their identities, which will affect their past, present, and future in dramatic and life-altering ways...</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_899061152" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/899061152" />
    <a title="Shell The Belle " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15880350-shell-the-belle"><img alt="Shell The Belle " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1399759491p2/15880350.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/899061152?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shell The Belle " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shell The Belle " href="/user/show/15880350-shell-the-belle">Shell The Belle </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone who likes a fast paced intrigue with a bit of romance thrown in. </span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Shell The Belle  by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/28967348-umm-r-the-bookworm">$umm£r  the Bookworm</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer899061152" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12309946180483385144"><b>4.75 Fantastic Sweet Sciencey And Could Well Be Happening Right Now STARS </b> <br/><br/><b>This is another book I read because my 14 year old daughter told me to! And I am so glad I did.</b><br/><br/>Sophie Mckenzie writes brilliantly and her stories are amazing. She draws you right into the story with her characters, their dialogue and the continual punchy chapters that <b>
  <i>always leave you wanting MORE!</i>
</b><br/><br/>The writing is brilliantly done, and although it does slow down for a few chapters in the middle, mostly it is quick paced</span>
  <span id="freeText12309946180483385144" style="display:none"><b>4.75 Fantastic Sweet Sciencey And Could Well Be Happening Right Now STARS </b> <br><br><b>This is another book I read because my 14 year old daughter told me to! And I am so glad I did.</b><br><br>Sophie Mckenzie writes brilliantly and her stories are amazing. She draws you right into the story with her characters, their dialogue and the continual punchy chapters that <b>
  <i>always leave you wanting MORE!</i>
</b><br><br>The writing is brilliantly done, and although it does slow down for a few chapters in the middle, mostly it is quick paced and full of intrigue that grabs you by your curiosity and holds you there for the entire ride.<br><br>The story centers around two 15 year olds, Theo and Rachel. It is told in duel perspective from them and each chapter is done in turn – and believe me, and the end of each chapter you are left desperate for next instalment.<br><br>The two teens find themselves inextricably linked by events surrounding both their births, and Theo instigates a meeting with Rachel to find out if she knows more than he does. She doesn’t, but that initial meeting brings forth a chaos that will threaten to destroy both of them and everything they knew and thought was real.<br><br>Theo is sweet and not at all cocky, heck the guy even blushes on occasion! <br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=6sxdax" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399554922ra/9566478.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>He is your typical teen boy, not really knowing what to do around a girl. He feels clumsy and awkward, and has absolutely no idea the effect he is having on Rachel. Yep, typical clueless dude!! <br><br><b>THEO</b><br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=28ip89d" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1399554009i/9566267._SY540_.png" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Rachel is also your typical teen girl; she has self-esteem issues, and takes far too personally jibes from the other girls at school. She also feels she is constantly being unfavourably compared to her dead sister, who died before Rachel was born. She thinks she’s fat, because her mother has an issue with what Rachel eats, and because some of the more popular/nasty girls tell her she is.<br><br><b>RACHEL</b><br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=20h398m" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1399554009i/9566268._SY540_.jpg" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>What is so fabulous about this book is <i>how</i> much both the characters of Theo and Rachel show real growth throughout the story and become much stronger, both physically and mentally, than either of them would ever have thought they could. Their attitudes to so many things change as they continue on their journey of not only what lies at the core of both their lives but also of beautiful self-discovery.<br><br>It was lovely to watch their relationship blossom, especially from Theo’s perspective. I totally love them both and cant wait to read more of them.<br><br>I would say that as an adult reading this, I had pretty much worked out a lot of the plot twists, but young teens will totally love this. And even though I had worked stuff out, it in no way distracted from my enjoyment of the story.<br><br>In fact, I think some of the twists were meant to be worked out by the reader pretty early on, because my 14 year old worked some of them out too - and you are almost shouting at the characters about it! <br><br><b>The science stuff surrounding Elijah and his work is incredibly current and totally believable. It could be happening right now!!!</b><br><br>The ending left you wanting <b>MORE</b> and I cant wait to start reading the sequel - Blood Ransom - I am so looking forward to more of Theo and Rachel and their continuing adventures.<br><br>All in all I would recommend this book to anyone, not only teens, who likes a good faced paced story with a bit of Romance thrown in to sweeten it. <br><br><b>A TOTALLY BRILLIANT READ. THANK YOU TO MY DAUGHTER. LOVE YOU SO MUCH.</b><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="12309946180483385144" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_471528862" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/471528862" />
    <a title="Rachael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14233130-rachael"><img alt="Rachael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1357073555p2/14233130.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/471528862?book_show_action=true">Dec 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachael" href="/user/show/14233130-rachael">Rachael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer471528862" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4600448085962142865">(Might be some spoilers!!!)<br/><br/>Sophie Mckenzie is one of my all-time favourite authors. I read many of her books when I was younger and I continue to read and reread them now. I could possibly stretch to say that the Blood Ties series is my favourite of hers, but I don't know, It's too hard!<br/>The characters are amazing, I love how much Rachel changes and how you can really feel it through-out the book. Also, the change in characters every chapter is genious. Not only can you see what they're both doin</span>
  <span id="freeText4600448085962142865" style="display:none">(Might be some spoilers!!!)<br /><br />Sophie Mckenzie is one of my all-time favourite authors. I read many of her books when I was younger and I continue to read and reread them now. I could possibly stretch to say that the Blood Ties series is my favourite of hers, but I don't know, It's too hard!<br />The characters are amazing, I love how much Rachel changes and how you can really feel it through-out the book. Also, the change in characters every chapter is genious. Not only can you see what they're both doing but you can also get their diferent opinions, which was really good with these characters. I was worried that Rachel and Theo would sound the same but I was presently surprised. I could easily pick up the book from where I'd left off and know instantly who was narrating.<br />The plot, which is full of scientific goodness, didn't disappoint. Just when you think the ation has ceased, another fight is set off. This was good because it didn't just mean one huge scene at the end. Personally, I prefer Sophie Mckenzie's sci-fi to her more romance novels, but coincidentally, that is because they're a mixture of both. Theo and Rachel's relationship was a great touch to the story, you were tied as much to that as you are the plot. <br />And finally, the writing was exceptional. As I said before, you could easily tell who was talking. The descriptions were exactly what you would excpect from the characters, instead of a deep description that is totally out of character.<br />Another great novel from Sophie Mckenzie, and maybe my favourite!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4600448085962142865" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_91640509" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/91640509" />
    <a title="Iffath" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2514541-iffath"><img alt="Iffath" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1469887209p2/2514541.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/91640509?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Iffath" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Iffath" href="/user/show/2514541-iffath">Iffath</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer91640509" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer378540069920111837">I thought that Blood Ties was a very challenging book because it's about cloning and wars. As this is a very rare subject, it was obvious that it would be different from Sophie’s other books. Blood Ties is about a Theo and Rachel who are the main characters. At first the two don’t know each other but as the story develops they meet, as Theo wants to learn more about his father after his mother, reveals that nearly all the things he thought he knew about his father, were lies. Theo wants to know </span>
  <span id="freeText378540069920111837" style="display:none">I thought that Blood Ties was a very challenging book because it's about cloning and wars. As this is a very rare subject, it was obvious that it would be different from Sophie’s other books. Blood Ties is about a Theo and Rachel who are the main characters. At first the two don’t know each other but as the story develops they meet, as Theo wants to learn more about his father after his mother, reveals that nearly all the things he thought he knew about his father, were lies. Theo wants to know why he has a bodyguard and attends a posh boy’s school when they live in a tiny house with worn-out furniture.<br />Rachel is the kind of person who is extremely nervous and self-conscious of herself. This may be explained because she is bullied because of her size. I liked this character because she wasn’t like one of those so-called ‘perfect’ girls, like Jemima, who had an ideal life. She also seems to live in the shadow of her sister Rebecca who died before Rachel was born. The fact that her parents are constantly are making comparisons between her and Rebecca doesn’t help the situation, but makes her feel even more depressed. <br />I thought this book flowed quite well and the book was very well thought out. I think that there wasn’t much descriptive language which could have given us a bit more of an image of what was going on. <br />One really good point about this book was I like how it ended – with Rachel and Theo not actually getting together because they are not allowed to know the exact location of the other to protect themselves. I liked this because it was less predictable and was a nice little twist.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="378540069920111837" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_410038066" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/410038066" />
    <a title="Katya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4324634-katya"><img alt="Katya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285183076p2/4324634.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/410038066?book_show_action=true">Sep 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katya" href="/user/show/4324634-katya">Katya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer410038066" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11465720284609869333">Unnecessary drama is the bane of my existence.<br/><br/><br/>Okay, not really, but it’s pretty high up the list, right there with forced romances and nonsensical motivations, though one can make the point about this being all unnecessary drama. How does this tie in with today’s pick? Simply put, it ruined a perfectly good premise.<br/><br/><br/>The pitch for “Blood Ties” is very ambiguous. Honestly, when I first saw it, the sci-fi aspect went completely in over my head. I knew there was a mystery, but not until the big revea</span>
  <span id="freeText11465720284609869333" style="display:none">Unnecessary drama is the bane of my existence.<br /><br /><br />Okay, not really, but it’s pretty high up the list, right there with forced romances and nonsensical motivations, though one can make the point about this being all unnecessary drama. How does this tie in with today’s pick? Simply put, it ruined a perfectly good premise.<br /><br /><br />The pitch for “Blood Ties” is very ambiguous. Honestly, when I first saw it, the sci-fi aspect went completely in over my head. I knew there was a mystery, but not until the big reveal, which is either a testament to McKenzie’s mastery as a writer or my own scatter-mindedness. Pick the one which suits you best.<br /><br /><br />I’ll admit, I had a hard time liking the two main characters, Rachel and Theo. The latter, I never really liked, mostly because of his tendency to wangst over ridiculous shit. Rachel, on the other hand, grew a lot on me - I did facepalm a lot, especially when she decided she’s in love with Theo, even when she knew he was using her, but then she grew into a much more kick-ass character, one that was willing to take risks and be in charge. I liked that.<br /><br /><br />What I didn’t like was how overwrought this whole thing is.<br /><br /><br />Here’s a scenario for you. You discover you are a clone. What do you do? Would you:<br /><br /><br />A/ Sit down in expectation of the inevitable identity crisis<br />B/ Inform yourself about the genetic illnesses and mutations that could result<br />C/ Freak out that you’re a Nazi, because your parents were Nazis<br /><br /><br />If you answered C, congratulations, you and Theo will get along just dandy. <br /><br /><br />Logicfail aside, the above example is just one of the few things that made Theo completely insufferable to me. So the guy discovers he’s a clone. I understand that he’s too immature to realize everything that comes with that, but out of all the soul-searching to be done, is ideology the best thing you could think of? Seriously? <br /><br /><br />Another thing I didn’t particularly like was his relationship with Rachel. As much as I rolled my eyes at her for throwing the “L” word around when the book wasn’t even through its halfway mark, I can’t really blame Rachel - she’s a teenage girl, a very lonely teenage girl, who has been bullied in school and at home and who has some understandable self-esteem issues. Why wouldn’t she latch onto the first guy who pays attention to her? <br /><br /><br />Theo, on the other hand, didn’t give two shits for her - not at first, and not later, though the text would have us think otherwise. He didn’t care for Rachel, except in terms of how she could get him what he wanted. He only started to care for her after she brought the freaking cavalry to his rescue, and after he suspected she might be crushing on someone else (in spite of that someone else being in a committed relationship, much older, and his friend. Because tension needs to happen.) At which point he was all: “Hey, Rachel’s hot. And she used to kind of be into me. Maybe I should make sure she still is.”<br /><br /><br />Yeah, no. Go to hell, Theo. And your fucking attitude too. <br /><br />For this review and more, come over to <a href="http://www.thebooklantern.com/2012/09/review-blood-ties-by-sophie-mckenzie.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Book Lantern</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11465720284609869333" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2262546942" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2262546942" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2262546942?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alicia McGorlick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alicia McGorlick" href="/user/show/63317626-alicia-mcgorlick">Alicia McGorlick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2262546942" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15586924015070761211">Quite a thrilling book, though Rachel's character initially irritated me, thank goodness the character grew strong and dependent! There was no real closure at the end which is a bit annoying... perhaps leaving room for a possible sequel (unsure if there is one or not... writing this review on the train). All in all, a book that at times I wanted to abandon and other times the plot grew interesting. If you like thrillers, love stories and scientific exploration this book is for you. A pretty good</span>
  <span id="freeText15586924015070761211" style="display:none">Quite a thrilling book, though Rachel's character initially irritated me, thank goodness the character grew strong and dependent! There was no real closure at the end which is a bit annoying... perhaps leaving room for a possible sequel (unsure if there is one or not... writing this review on the train). All in all, a book that at times I wanted to abandon and other times the plot grew interesting. If you like thrillers, love stories and scientific exploration this book is for you. A pretty good read!</span>

<div id="review_294232545" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/294232545" />
    <a title="Discombobulatedbooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8195280-discombobulatedbooks"><img alt="Discombobulatedbooks" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/294232545?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Discombobulatedbooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Discombobulatedbooks" href="/user/show/8195280-discombobulatedbooks">Discombobulatedbooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Young YA readers, people who want an easy book to read</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8195280-discombobulatedbooks?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer294232545" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11005614958834402382">MAY CONTAIN MINOR SPOILERS!!! (I have tried to keep out as many spoilers as possible… but there are still a few in there; such as who ends up with who… and stuff…) <br/>I first started reading this book because I saw it was written by Sophie McKenzie, who has also written Girl, Missing. I really enjoyed reading Girl, Missing, and after reading this, I felt that this book was a bit of a let down. I felt that the plot didn’t flow very fast and it sometimes got side- tracked. The characters sometimes go</span>
  <span id="freeText11005614958834402382" style="display:none">MAY CONTAIN MINOR SPOILERS!!! (I have tried to keep out as many spoilers as possible… but there are still a few in there; such as who ends up with who… and stuff…) <br />I first started reading this book because I saw it was written by Sophie McKenzie, who has also written Girl, Missing. I really enjoyed reading Girl, Missing, and after reading this, I felt that this book was a bit of a let down. I felt that the plot didn’t flow very fast and it sometimes got side- tracked. The characters sometimes got on my nerves; it might be because the book was written by an adult; so of course she just had to make the characters stereotypical, especially Rachel, “a typical teenager” which meant that all she really cared about was how she looked, etc. But that’s about the end of my small rant! I think that the plot itself is actually really good!- I liked the twists, but I’m not sure i would actually call them twists because I saw them coming awhile off…, but maybe that’s just me, because I’m not entirely the most normal person in the world… <br />(You can tell by the amount of I use!)<br />Even so, I still enjoyed the book; it was quite good, just not amazing, or mind- blowing. But still good. If it wasn’t I wouldn’t have finished it.<br />Summary<br />This book evolves around two characters; Theo and Rachel. They find themselves the target of an evil group of people, so of course, like any sane person; they run away! However, unlike any sane person, they run away into another group of bad people… who are just the littlest bit creepy…, only a little So basically the book is about Theo and Rachel running away and trying to survive!<br />Cons<br />The Romanticness (Romance? Romanocity? Romantication?)<br />I didn’t like how most of Rachels thoughts were about Theo. I sometimes felt like screaming “GET A GRIP ON YOURSELF” because she is portrayed as “a typical teenage girl” which just drives me nuts… Most of her thoughts were like “Will Theo like this dress I’m wearing?” or “Am I flirting too much with Theo?” instead of thinking “HOW THE HELL AM I GOING TO NOT DIE?” She was just sometimes so selfish… though I have to admit that she does develop throughout the book- at the end she did think about other people, not just herself. And it’s probably not very realistic to think about what a boy is thinking of you, than if you’re gonna live. Just saying.<br />The End<br />Let me just get this out of my system: “OMG THE END!!! I HATE IT… IT WASN’T SATISFYING AND IT WAS JUST LEFT SO BROAD (I would say what but I’m trying to keep this review relatively spoiler free )” I hated the fact that *** dies… ;( It just made me feel so sorry for *** because finally when they are just about to win, then die… right at the end… its so sad… but I guess this is a twist that I didnt see… I guess it’s quite a good twist!- i hust wish that Sophie McKenzie had made that part more dramatic and had dragged the moment out more. Getting back to the End…; I hated the fact that the bad guy got away… during the last few pages I was looking thinking “Why isn’t he dead yet???, There are only a few more pages left…?” There wasn’t any proper closure to the book and I felt so sorry for *** because he was just so alone… with a potential killer…. and he was so scared before… ;( I wish we had gotten to know him properly; it all felt a little rushed…<br />Pros<br />The two different perspectives<br />I really liked how Sophie McKenzie wrote the books in two different view points! It makes the characters more real, in a way… kinda…, well as much as a book can be real. It was amusing watching them think about what the other person thought about them then panicking.<br />The development of the characters<br />I loved how we saw the characters develop. I’ll start with Rachel, because she is the character who developed more straight forwardly. Rachel, at the beginning of the book, was a shy and ugly girl who always got pushed around, and at the end of the book she was none of those things. I loved how she used to doubt herself so much, and then gradually, she began to get more confident and she believed in herself more and she was sure of who she was. I liked how Sophie McKenzie did the last ever chapter of the book; how we saw her starting a new school with a completely different personality. Theo… He’s more difficult to explain. We still see him develop as a character… but he also goes downhill for a time… especially after he finds out about his parents… ;( But towards the end he was also a changed person; maybe not as much as Rachel, but still changed.<br />Favourite Quotes<br />To be honest, this book doesn’t have many really good quotes… there are a few funny ones though, but unintentionally funny…<br />“I dropped to my knees and puked over the tarmac. I sat back on my heels, shivering, and wiped my mouth on my sleeve. “What a waste of Mel’s delicious food”<br />“I resisted the temptation to bite his head off”<br />Overall<br />I think this is quite a good book. I wouldn’t say it was awesome or spectacular, but it was a good plot and the characters are kinda likeable (because what’s worse than reading a book where you hate all of the characters! actually I can think of a few…).<br />I would say that this book is probably a three, maybe three and a half, star book. It would have been higher if the twists weren’t so predictable, but anyway, I enjoyed it and I would recommend it to any of you guys out there who might read this blog! <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://discombobulatedbooks.wordpress.com/">http://discombobulatedbooks.wordpress...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11005614958834402382" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_71282579" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/71282579" />
    <a title="Kelly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1803230-kelly"><img alt="Kelly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1278898706p2/1803230.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/71282579?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly" href="/user/show/1803230-kelly">Kelly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer71282579" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14650492830502318402">All Theo knows about his dad is that he died when the clinic he was working at was bombed. That is until his mum lets slip that his dad is still alive and in hiding. Theo is determined to find him, and his search leads him to Rachel, together they try to solve the mystery surrounding their births and the clinic their parents worked at, but what they find completely blows their lives apart...<br/><br/>This was surprisingly good, much better than I imagined it would be. The plot is enjoyable, with lots of a</span>
  <span id="freeText14650492830502318402" style="display:none">All Theo knows about his dad is that he died when the clinic he was working at was bombed. That is until his mum lets slip that his dad is still alive and in hiding. Theo is determined to find him, and his search leads him to Rachel, together they try to solve the mystery surrounding their births and the clinic their parents worked at, but what they find completely blows their lives apart...<br /><br />This was surprisingly good, much better than I imagined it would be. The plot is enjoyable, with lots of action and little twists to the story, which you never expect. As it's written for teens the writing is simple, but that doesn't detract from the story at all. Theo and Rachel are likeable, well written characters, that you connect with very easily. Overall it's a great young adult thriller, and I'm looking forward to reading more by this author. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14650492830502318402" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3617234915" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3617234915" />
    <a title="KAT2020" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/119475986-kat2020"><img alt="KAT2020" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3617234915?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="KAT2020" class="user" itemprop="url" name="KAT2020" href="/user/show/119475986-kat2020">KAT2020</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3617234915" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2020427818445526765">This was a very gripping book with a great plot.<br/>This book is about two 15-year-old teenagers, Rachel and Theo, who both have problems. Theo has a bodyguard without knowing why, goes to a very expensive private school but lives in a shabby house, and has a father who he thought was dead but is apparently alive. Rachel has incredibly old parents and is constantly compared to her stylish sister Rebecca, who died before she was born. Theo finds a news article that leads him to Rachel’s dad and an ex</span>
  <span id="freeText2020427818445526765" style="display:none">This was a very gripping book with a great plot.<br />This book is about two 15-year-old teenagers, Rachel and Theo, who both have problems. Theo has a bodyguard without knowing why, goes to a very expensive private school but lives in a shabby house, and has a father who he thought was dead but is apparently alive. Rachel has incredibly old parents and is constantly compared to her stylish sister Rebecca, who died before she was born. Theo finds a news article that leads him to Rachel’s dad and an extremely controversial geneticist, Elijah Lazio. He finds Rachel and persuades her to bring her dad’s laptop to check for emails between her dad and a man named Lewis. They find an email, but it substitutes some of the real names for the names of Greek gods. They manage to work out that Apollo is Theo and Artemis is Rachel. The email mentions a plan to ‘shut Apollo up’ so Theo decides to run to Germany, where he believes his father is. However, just when Theo and Rachel set off, an organization almost kills them, and they realize that they are not safe. The man who saved them reveals that he is Lewis and drives them to Scotland, where Theo is promised that he will meet his dad. Theo finally meets his dad, but he is not who he thinks he is, and both Theo and Rachel learn horrifying secrets about their births. <br />In this book, the chapters alternated between Theo and Rachel’s perspectives, which I liked because they were separated quite often, and major events were happening to both at the same time. There was lots of action and plot twists. It had a sci-fi context but was more like a thriller because it did not go into a lot of detail in the scientific parts. The pace was good: fast enough to keep me guessing but not so fast that I could not follow. However, there was one section in the middle that did not have a lot of action and went at a relatively slow pace. I also thought that the main problem happened quite close to the end so there was not a lot of detail about it.<br />I would recommend this book to readers of 11+. It is a bit confusing to begin with but once you get sucked in, it makes sense.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2020427818445526765" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2339563944" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2339563944" />
    <a title="jobeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49233524-jobeth"><img alt="jobeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534336338p2/49233524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2339563944?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jobeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jobeth" href="/user/show/49233524-jobeth">jobeth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2339563944" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12092752157108253724">Sigh, this had so much potential. The idea is really interesting but I think the way the significant events of the story was painted lacked a sense of originality. I felt that it was so predictable.<br/><br/>One thing I truly loved was the relationship between Mel and Lewis. I loved these two characters more than the actual main characters. The protagonists (Theo & Rachel) had me rolling my eyes so many times. Honestly, I don't know why the author portrayed a jealous Theo who thinks Rachel had feelings fo</span>
  <span id="freeText12092752157108253724" style="display:none">Sigh, this had so much potential. The idea is really interesting but I think the way the significant events of the story was painted lacked a sense of originality. I felt that it was so predictable.<br /><br />One thing I truly loved was the relationship between Mel and Lewis. I loved these two characters more than the actual main characters. The protagonists (Theo &amp; Rachel) had me rolling my eyes so many times. Honestly, I don't know why the author portrayed a jealous Theo who thinks Rachel had feelings for Lewis when this said person is way older than Rachel. That was weird.</span>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('z4WKOURr/Nu4RC/E0Xl12AegWvRou0FvXVsok0LIdEo6qvTRISzLY+aMpFKwclaileRzQpntFvuRijwXQcbSrg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KiY1VG5mYS33Yh50U4io9xvkrFAdq47wYKFrW+FfT0XfCUu8CyFWlamqleIyg4uNiaCF5uz92WSscH/f4lHpoQ==')})
  }
//]]>

This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
